	<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Devon heraldry</h1>
	
	<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
		<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Powderham_Castle,_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2097" data-file-width="3066" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Powderham_Castle%2C_2009.jpg/220px-Powderham_Castle%2C_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Powderham_Castle%2C_2009.jpg/330px-Powderham_Castle%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Powderham_Castle%2C_2009.jpg/440px-Powderham_Castle%2C_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Powderham_Castle,_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The arms of <a href="/wiki/House_of_Courtenay" title="House of Courtenay">Courtenay</a> on display above <a href="/wiki/Powderham_Castle" title="Powderham Castle">Powderham Castle</a> in Devon in 2015, a seat of that family since the 14th century</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG/220px-Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG/330px-Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG/440px-Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fortescue_BannerOfArms_FilleighChurch_Devon.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fortescue <a href="/wiki/Banner_of_arms" title="Banner of arms">banner of arms</a> in the Fortescue Chapel of St Paul's Church, <a href="/wiki/Filleigh" title="Filleigh">Filleigh</a>, Devon. The Fortescue family (<a href="/wiki/Earl_Fortescue" title="Earl Fortescue">Earl Fortescue</a>) were lords of the manor of Filleigh, in which parish is situated their former seat, <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Filleigh" title="Castle Hill, Filleigh">Castle Hill</a>. The last Fortescue to own Castle Hill was Lady Margaret Fortescue (1923-2013), eldest daughter and co-heiress of <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Fortescue,_5th_Earl_Fortescue" title="Hugh Fortescue, 5th Earl Fortescue">Hugh Fortescue, 5th Earl Fortescue</a> (1888-1958), although now owned by her daughter Eleanor, Countess of Arran (née van Cutsem) who lives there with her husband <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Arran" title="Earl of Arran">Arthur Gore, 9th Earl of Arran</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Landed_gentry" title="Landed gentry">landed gentry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Devonshire" title="Devonshire">Devonshire</a>, like the rest of the English and European gentry, bore <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldic arms</a> from the start of the age of heraldry <i>circa</i> 1200-1215. The fashion for the display of heraldry ceased about the end of the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> (1901) by which time most of the ancient armigerous families of Devonshire had died out, moved away or parted with their landed estates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> 
</p><p>In 2015 a very few ancient families remain in the county represented by direct male descendants, most notably <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Devon" title="Earl of Devon">Courtenay</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manor_of_Powderham" title="Manor of Powderham">Powderham</a>, Fulford of <a href="/wiki/Great_Fulford" title="Great Fulford">Fulford</a>,  Kelly of Kelly, Cruwys of <a href="/wiki/Cruwys_Morchard" title="Cruwys Morchard">Cruwys Morchard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baron_Clifford" title="Baron Clifford">Clifford</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chudleigh" title="Chudleigh">Chudleigh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acland_Baronets" title="Acland Baronets">Acland</a> of <a href="/wiki/Killerton" title="Killerton">Killerton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broadclyst" title="Broadclyst">Broadclyst</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrey_Baronets" title="Wrey Baronets">Wrey</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tawstock" title="Tawstock">Tawstock</a>, etc. A few ancient Devon estates are still owned by descendants via female lines, for example <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Filleigh" title="Castle Hill, Filleigh">Castle Hill, Filleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manor_of_Molland" title="Manor of Molland">Molland</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incledon,_Braunton" title="Incledon, Braunton">Incledon, Braunton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hall,_Bishop%27s_Tawton" title="Hall, Bishop's Tawton">Hall, Bishop's Tawton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newnham_Park" title="Newnham Park">Newnham Park</a>, etc. In most cases the laws of English heraldry preclude the transmission of paternal armorials via a female heiress (other than in the form of <a href="/wiki/Quartering_(heraldry)" title="Quartering (heraldry)">quartering</a>), thus most of these inheritors via female lines, generally deriving from the same pool of high-status English armigerous families, bring their own paternal heraldry, possibly previously foreign to Devon, to the estates inherited. 
</p><p>For example, the Irish arms of Gore (<a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Arran" title="Earl of Arran">Earl of Arran</a>) are now associated with <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Filleigh" title="Castle Hill, Filleigh">Castle Hill, Filleigh</a>, until 1958 the seat of the last male representative of the <a href="/wiki/Earl_Fortescue" title="Earl Fortescue">Fortescue family</a> which originated in Devon in the 12th century. In a few cases however, male heirs via female lines have been required by the legator to seek royal licence to adopt his own arms and surname, otherwise destined to disappearance, in lieu of the legatees own. This was the case with the families most notably of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rolle" title="Mark Rolle">Rolle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basset_family" title="Basset family">Basset</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stucley_Baronets" title="Stucley Baronets">Stucley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradfield_House" title="Bradfield House">Walrond</a>, etc.
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Standard_sources">Standard sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Standard sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <p>The standard sources for students of the <b>heraldry of Devon</b> are as follows:
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Documents">Documents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Documents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Heraldic_visitation" title="Heraldic visitation">Heraldic Visitations</a> of Devon: <a href="/wiki/John_Lambrick_Vivian" title="John Lambrick Vivian">Vivian, Lt.Col. J.L.</a>, (Ed.) The Visitations of the County of Devon: Comprising the Heralds' Visitations of 1531, 1564 &amp; 1620, Exeter, 1895.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole, Sir William</a> (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_de_la_Pole,_6th_Baronet" title="Sir John de la Pole, 6th Baronet">Sir John-William de la Pole</a> (ed.), London, 1791:
<ul><li>"The Armes of such nobles and gentlemen which have anciently dwelled &amp; had lands in Devonshire", pp. 444–467;</li>
<li>"An alphabet of the armes of the gentlemen of Devonshire as well of those being as of those which have bine", pp. 467–510;</li></ul></li>
<li>The Notebook of <a href="/wiki/Tristram_Risdon" title="Tristram Risdon">Tristram Risdon</a> (d.1640)<a class="external autonumber" href="https://archive.org/stream/notebookoftristr00risdrich/notebookoftristr00risdrich_djvu.txt" rel="nofollow">[23]</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_Lysons" title="Samuel Lysons">Lysons, Samuel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Lysons_(antiquarian)" title="Daniel Lysons (antiquarian)">Lysons, Daniel</a>,  <a class="external text" href="http://www.british-history.ac.uk/report.aspx?compid=50555" rel="nofollow">Magna Britannia, Volume 6: <i>Devonshire</i>, London, 1822</a>:
<ul><li>Ancient Families, of which the principal Branch is extinct, or removed, since 1620, yet some of the Descendants remain in the County.</li>
<li>Families known, or supposed, to be extinct since 1620, or removed out of the County.</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Prince_(biographer)" title="John Prince (biographer)">Prince, John</a>, (1643–1723) The Worthies of Devon, 1810 edition, "Arms, Crests and Mottoes of the Families treated of in this Work", blazons pp. 779–85 &amp; plates I-V following: "Arms" (monochrome depictions of 145 shields)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sabine_Baring-Gould" title="Sabine Baring-Gould">Baring-Gould, Sabine</a> &amp; Twigge, Robert, <i>An Armory of the Western Counties (Devon and Cornwall): From the Unpublished Manuscripts of the XVI Century</i>, published by J.G. Commin, 1898 <a class="external autonumber" href="https://archive.org/stream/anarmorywestern00twiggoog#page/n4/mode/2up" rel="nofollow">[24]</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Carew,_1st_Earl_of_Totnes" title="George Carew, 1st Earl of Totnes">Carew, Sir George</a> (1555-1629) (created in 1626 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earl_of_Totnes" title="Earl of Totnes">Earl of Totnes</a>), <i>Carew's Scroll of Arms 1588, Collected from Churches in Devonshire etc., with Additions from Joseph Holland's Collection of Arms 1579</i>, Exeter, 1901. ( See also: Devon &amp; Cornwall Notes and Queries, Vol. 1, pt. 2)</li>
<li>Colby, Rev. Frederick T., <i>The Heraldry of Exeter</i><a class="external autonumber" href="http://archaeologydataservice.ac.uk/archiveDS/archiveDownload?t=arch-1132-1/dissemination/pdf/030/030_235_263.pdf" rel="nofollow">[25]</a>; See also: Westcote, Thomas, <i>View of Devonshire</i>, Chap. XV <a class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=WJGEAAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA149&amp;lpg=PA149&amp;dq=blundell+paly+of+five+gules+and+argent&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=dGLbRq7SLm&amp;sig=p7zB8_2ZdP5bscZ75DqyXMkE4tE&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwjAkeWsxrjTAhVMJFAKHWsSBnEQ6AEIMTAB#v=onepage&amp;q=blundell%20paly%20of%20five%20gules%20and%20argent&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">[26]</a>, list of arms in <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Guildhall" title="Exeter Guildhall">Exeter Guildhall</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Observation">Observation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Observation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Original_research plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Original_research" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>possibly contains <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">original research</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verifying</a> the claims made and adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a>. Statements consisting only of original research should be removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Observation of surviving monuments in parish churches and mansion houses. As for the arms of Courtenay: "the stamp of whose almost princely authority may be extensively recognised throughout the county" (Davidson).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Frequently discrepancies between these sources exist. Painted monuments in parish churches often have been restored, in some cases several times over the centuries, and the arms depicted may not be as originally painted. Heraldry sculpted in relief on stone is liable to wear and crumbling, especially when placed in the favourite location, exposed to the elements for centuries, on the porch or gatehouse of the family mansion. Ancient <a href="/wiki/Monumental_brass" title="Monumental brass">monumental brasses</a> do not show tinctures but otherwise provide lasting records of heraldry. Stained glass depictions are optimal sources as they include tinctures, but ancient survivals are rare. Mural monuments placed high up on walls generally survive vandalism of past ages whilst paintings of arms on escutcheons sculpted in stone on mediaeval <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_tomb" title="Chest tomb">chest tombs</a> have rarely survived and often were "scraped" clean of all decoration in the 17th century. Heraldic monuments displaying a family's arms are generally found in the church of the parish in which is situated their seat, but the paternal arms may also be found in remoter parish churches where a daughter of the family has married into a family resident there. In such a case the arms are shown <a href="/wiki/Impalement_(heraldry)" title="Impalement (heraldry)">impaled</a> by the arms of her husband. Clearly the greatest problems in tracing heraldry relate to long extinct families. A few ancient Devon families survive, such as the Fortescues, and a flag showing the Fortescue arms still flies above <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Filleigh" title="Castle Hill, Filleigh">Castle Hill</a> in 2013. There is no shortage of surviving examples of the arms of the Chichesters and Rolles, but surviving heraldry of the ancient Courtenay Earls of Devon seated at Tiverton Castle is rare, although frequently shown as <a href="/wiki/Quartering_(heraldry)" title="Quartering (heraldry)">quarterings</a> in the arms of related families.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Devon_arms">List of Devon arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: List of Devon arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</p>

<td>Yonge<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>

<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yonge_(OfColebrooke)_Arms.svg"><img alt="Yonge (OfColebrooke) Arms.svg" data-file-height="847" data-file-width="737" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Yonge_%28OfColebrooke%29_Arms.svg/70px-Yonge_%28OfColebrooke%29_Arms.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Yonge_%28OfColebrooke%29_Arms.svg/105px-Yonge_%28OfColebrooke%29_Arms.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Yonge_%28OfColebrooke%29_Arms.svg/140px-Yonge_%28OfColebrooke%29_Arms.svg.png 2x" width="70"/></a>

<td><i>Per fess sable and argent, three lions rampant guardant counterchanged</i>

<td>Landsend,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><a href="/wiki/Colebrooke,_Devon" title="Colebrooke, Devon">Colebrooke</a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Blazons_by_Sir_William_Pole">Blazons by Sir William Pole</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Blazons by Sir William Pole">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following blazons, with spellings corrected and modernised,  were recorded by Sir William Pole:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks" role="note">This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Devon_heraldry&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a>.</div>
<ul><li>Abbot, of <a href="/wiki/Hartland,_Devon" title="Hartland, Devon">Hartland</a>:<i>Or, a cross voided between four eaglets displayed sable</i></li>
<li>Adiston, of Adeston: <i>Argent, a fess between three pellets</i></li>
<li>Affeton, of <a href="/wiki/Manor_of_Affeton" title="Manor of Affeton">Affeton</a>: <i>Argent, a chevron engrailed between three fleurs-de-lys sable</i></li>
<li>Acland, of <a href="/wiki/Acland,_Landkey" title="Acland, Landkey">Acland</a>: <i>Barry argent and sable, two pales counterchanged a fess gules over all</i></li>
<li>Alabaster, of <a href="/wiki/Bicton,_Devon" title="Bicton, Devon">Bicton</a>: <i>Azure, three cross-bows bent or</i></li>
<li>Alley, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Exeter" title="Bishop of Exeter">Bishop of Exeter</a>: <i>Azure, a pale engrailed between two lions rampant ermine crowned or</i></li>
<li>Ameredith, of Pole: <i>Argent, a lion rampant sable collared and chained gules</i></li>
<li>Aller, of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aller,_South_Molton&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aller, South Molton (page does not exist)">Aller</a>: <i>Argent, three parrots vert 2 and 1 beaked and membered gules</i></li>
<li>Arundell, of Hempston Arundell: <i>Sable, six swallows (martlets) argent 3,2,1</i></li>
<li>Arundell of Hempston Arundell: <i>Argent, six swallows sable, 3,2,1</i></li>
<li>Arthur, of Weston_Super_Mare: <i>Gules, a chevron between three clarions</i></li>
<li>Ank of Anke: <i>Gules, two bars three annulets in chief argent</i></li>
<li>Ayshford of Ayshford: <i>Argent, three ash crops vert between two chevrons sable</i></li>
<li>Ashlegh of Ashlegh: <i>...a pheon...</i></li>
<li>Ashton of Ashton: <i>Vert, three bends argent</i></li>
<li>Ashthorp of Sampford Peverell: <i>...a bend...</i></li>
<li>Amidas of Plymouth: <i>Azure, a chevron argent between three acorn stalks and leaves or</i></li>
<li>Appleton: <i>Or a chevron sable between three apples vert</i></li>
<li>Ashenden of Dartmouth: <i>Argent, a lion rampant gules collared or</i></li>
<li>Atcomb of Atcombe: <i>Sable, three wings argent</i></li>
<li>Atwill of Exeter: <i>Argent, a chevron sable a pile in point counterchanged</i></li>
<li>Appeldor: <i>Gules, a fess undee argent</i></li>
<li>Atwill: <i>Argent, a fess three piles in chief</i></li>
<li>Atway: <i>... on a chief three lion's heads erased over-all a bend</i></li>
<li>Archdeacon of Haccombe: <i>Argent, three chevrons sable</i></li>
<li>Audleigh of Tawstock, (feudal) baron of Barnstaple and Dartington: <i>Gules fretty or</i></li>
<li>Avenell of Shepewas (Sheepwash): <i>Three spread-eaglets</i> (<i>Three eagles displayed</i>)</li>
<li>Avenell of Loxbere: <i>Argent, five fusils in fess sable between two barrulets gules</i></li>
<li>Auncell: <i>Ermine, a fess sable between a demi-lion in chief and three fusils in base 2 and 1 gules</i></li>
<li>Arscott of Dunsland: <i>Ermine, on a chief azure two buck's heads cabossed or</i></li>
<li>Atwill: <i>Argent, three leopard's faces azure</i></li>
<li>Atwood: <i>Sable semee of acorns or, a lion rampant argent</i></li>
<li>Basset of <a href="/wiki/Stevenstone" title="Stevenstone">Stevenstone</a> and Beaupire: <i>Argent, a chevron azure between three bugle horns sable</i></li>
<li>Bathe or Bathon, of Colbrooke: <i>Ermine, a bend gules</i></li>
<li>Bastard of Efford: <i>Or, a chevron azure</i></li>
<li>Basset of Umberleigh: <i>Barry undée of six or and gules</i></li>
<li>Batten of Dunsland: <i>Argent, three battle axes erect azure</i></li>
<li>Batten of Exeter: <i>Argent, a chevron between three battle axes erect azure</i></li>
<li>Bawceyn of Washborn Bawceyne: <i>Argent, two bars undée gules a quarter sable</i></li>
<li>Barry of Winscott: <i>Barry of six argent and gules</i></li>
<li>Battishull of Westwike: <i>Azure, a saltire crosslet between four owls argent</i></li>
<li>Bamfild (Bampfield): <i>Or, on a bend gules three mullets argent</i></li>
<li>Bamfild (Bampfield): <i>Paly of six or and vert on a bend gules three mullets argent</i></li>
<li>Baker: <i>Argent, on a saltire engrailed sable five escallops argent on a chief of the second a lion passant argent</i></li>
<li>Barron of Buckland Barron: <i>Argent, a chevron between three men's hearts sable</i></li>
<li>Barnhous of Kingston: <i>Gules, two wings conjoined in lure argent</i></li>
<li>Bawcomb of Bawcombe: <i>Argent, three bats displayed sable</i></li>
<li>Barkley or Bartlet of ... : <i>Sable, a fess ermine between three escallops argent</i></li>
<li>Balun of ... : <i>Barry dancetty of six argent and gules</i></li>
<li>Baunton of Combaunton (Combe Baunton): <i>Gules, a bend between three escallops or one in chief two in base</i></li>
<li>Bale of ... : <i>Argent, two bars gules between three mullets sable</i></li>
<li>Beandyn of ... : <i>Azure, on a bend or three torteaux</i></li>
<li>Beaudyn: <i>... , a chevron between three martlets</i></li>
<li>Beaumont of Yolston (Youlston): <i>Barry of six vairy and gules</i></li>
<li>Beaumont of Sebrescot: <i>Barry of six vairy and gules a bezant on the second bar</i></li>
<li>Beauchamp of Ryme: <i>Vairy, a label of three points gules</i></li>
<li>Beaupell(Beauple) of Knoweston (Knowstone): <i>Gules, a bend vairy cotised or</i></li>
<li>Beaupell(Beauple) of Knoweston (Knowstone) (<i>sic</i>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Beaple" title="Richard Beaple">Richard Beaple</a> Mayor of Barnstaple): <i>Gules, a bend vairy between six escallops argent</i></li>
<li>Bellew of Ashe Rogus (<a href="/wiki/Ash,_Braunton" title="Ash, Braunton">Ash, Braunton</a>): <i>Sable fretty or</i></li></ul>

The arms however of Butler of Parkham are the arms of Butler, Earl of Ormond (<i>Gules, three covered cups or</i>) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Difference_(heraldry)" title="Difference (heraldry)">differenced</a> with a field <i>azure</i>.</span>

<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vivian, p.284, with obvious printer's error ("Az" in place of "Ar") in that the field is given erroneously as <i>azure</i>, with a fess also <i>azure</i>, in contravention of the "<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rule_of_Tinctures&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rule of Tinctures (page does not exist)">Rule of Tinctures</a>", and would not show fully against the same background. Pole (p.480) gives the field as <i>argent</i>, but gives the location of the crescents incorrectly as on the fess. A relief-sculpted image of these arms survives on the large monument of <a href="/wiki/John_Chichester_(died_1569)" title="John Chichester (died 1569)">John Chichester (died 1569)</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raleigh,_Pilton" title="Raleigh, Pilton">Raleigh, Pilton</a>, Devon, see image:<a href="/wiki/File:HeraldicPanelChichesterMonumentPiltonDevon1569.JPG" title="File:HeraldicPanelChichesterMonumentPiltonDevon1569.JPG">File:HeraldicPanelChichesterMonumentPiltonDevon1569.JPG</a>, which shows the correct arrangement of the crescents and estoiles, although the tincture of the field has been wrongly re-painted as <i>or</i></span>

<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Richard_Polwhele" title="Richard Polwhele">Polwhele, Richard</a>, <i>History of Devonshire</i>, 3 Vols., Vol.2, London, 1793, Vol.2, p.183</span>

<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gilbert: <i>Argent, on a chevron gules three roses of the field</i>. These are the ancient arms of the family, as evidenced on monuments in Marldon Church 1496 and 1530 and in Churston Ferrers Church c.1575 (Source: Burke's Landed Gentry, 1937, p.886). In the 1620 Heraldic Visitation of Devon by <a href="/wiki/William_Camden" title="William Camden">William Camden</a>, Clarenceux King of Arms, the following arms were allowed to Raleigh Gilbert (1584-1634) of Compton: <i>Ermine, on a chevron sable three roses argent</i>. (Source: Burke's Landed Gentry, 1937, p.886). The family's arms are very confused, for example as given in Vivian, p.405: <i>Or, on a chevron sable three roses of the field leaved proper a bordure gules</i>. Pole, p.484, gives: <i>Argent, on a chevron sable three roses of the field</i></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Henry Harewood (d.1631) by his will donated £100 as the "Harewood Gift", a charity for the poor of South Molton (Report of the Commissioners Appointed ...: To Inquire Concerning Charities ..., 1825, pp.125-6 <a class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=t4JPAQAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA125&amp;lpg=PA125&amp;dq=harewood+south+molton&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=rGnZIfnbpq&amp;sig=kRUeDE2z5exh1qfET6lxCcsrsyc&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwiZxbXouOvUAhVJDMAKHbVUCE8Q6AEIQTAE#v=onepage&amp;q=harewood%20south%20molton&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">[7]</a>)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pole, p.487; as seen on monument of <a href="/wiki/Elize_Hele" title="Elize Hele">Elize Hele</a> (1560–1635) in <a href="/wiki/Bovey_Tracey" title="Bovey Tracey">Bovey Tracey</a> Church</span>

<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The family of Hext resided at a place named "Kingston", which although <a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole</a> (d.1635) suggests (almost as a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post_scriptum" title="Post scriptum">post scriptum</a></i>) is Kingston in the parish of Staverton (<i>"At Kingston their also dwelled Thomas Hext in King Edw 4 tyme"</i> (<a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole, Sir William</a> (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_de_la_Pole,_6th_Baronet" title="Sir John de la Pole, 6th Baronet">Sir John-William de la Pole</a> (ed.), London, 1791, p.277), cannot be reconciled with the well documented contemporaneous tenure of Kingston, Staverton, by the Barnhous family, whose heiress is known to have married John Rowe of Totnes. (During the reign of King Edward IV (1461-1483) "Kingston" was the seat of Thomas Hext, (<a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole, Sir William</a> (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_de_la_Pole,_6th_Baronet" title="Sir John de la Pole, 6th Baronet">Sir John-William de la Pole</a> (ed.), London, 1791, p.277; Vivian, p.484, pedigree of <i>Hext of Kingston</i>) one of whose daughters, Agnes Hext, married Sir <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Pollard" title="Lewis Pollard">Lewis Pollard</a> (Vivian, p.598, pedigree of Pollard) (c.1465-1526) of <a href="/wiki/Grilstone,_Bishop%27s_Nympton" title="Grilstone, Bishop's Nympton">Grilstone</a> in the parish of <a href="/wiki/Bishop%27s_Nympton" title="Bishop's Nympton">Bishop's Nympton</a>, Devon, <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Common_Pleas" title="Justice of the Common Pleas">Justice of the Common Pleas</a> from 1514 to 1526 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_George_Hoskins" title="William George Hoskins">Hoskins, W.G.</a>, A New Survey of England: Devon, London, 1959 (first published 1954), p.338) and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a> for <a href="/wiki/Totnes_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Totnes (UK Parliament constituency)">Totnes</a> in 1491) There is however a parish and village named <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Devon" title="Kingston, Devon">Kingston</a> in South Devon, about 14 miles south-west of Kingston, Staverton, and Thomas Hext "of Kingston", the first member of the family recorded in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heraldic_Visitations" title="Heraldic Visitations">Heraldic Visitations</a> of Devon, married a member of the <a href="/wiki/Earl_Fortescue" title="Earl Fortescue">Fortescue family</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whympston,_Modbury" title="Whympston, Modbury">Whympston, Modbury</a>, about 2 1/2 miles north-west of the village of Kingston.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Preston family of Devon was a junior branch of the <i>de Preston</i> family which during the reign of King Henry II (1154-1189) was seated at Preston Richard and Preston Patrick in Westmorland. On 1 April 1644  George Preston (of same ancient descent, same arms) was created a baronet "of Furness in the County of Lancaster". (Burke, Bernard, <i>Genealogical and Heraldic History of the Extinct and Dormant Baronetcies ...</i>, 2nd ed, 1844, pp.424 et seq <a class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=j3Q-AQAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA427&amp;lpg=PA427&amp;dq=preston+baronets+westmorland&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=CRWW82cJXc&amp;sig=ywGeXG7EYaSBeECMx9Kc2sVvBTk&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwjHk-XdutbQAhVrJcAKHQu6BeA4ChDoAQgfMAE#v=onepage&amp;q=preston%20baronets%20westmorland&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">[13]</a>)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Members of this family include Richard Prouse (d.1608), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Exeter" title="Mayor of Exeter">Mayor of Exeter</a>, and his son John Prouse (d.1624/5), Mayor of Exeter in 1620, whose memorial exists in Exeter Cathedral (Vivian, p.628, "MI")</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">per Pole, Sir William (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, Sir John-William de la Pole (ed.), London, 1791, p.498. Alternatively: <i>Ermine, a chevron gules a chief azure fretty or</i> (per Vivian,  p.631, pedigree of Prye of Horwell). These arms are visible on the monument to John Wrey (d.1597) in Tawstock Church, Devon. John Wrey's son Edmond Wrey married Katherine Prye, daughter of Roger Prye of Horwell (Vivian, p.631)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This family was the heir of Coffin of Portledge, Alwington, Devon, and in 1796 assumed the additional surname and arms of Coffin, resulting in the name Pine-Coffin (Vivian, p.211)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Rosemary_Lauder" title="Rosemary Lauder">Lauder, Rosemary</a>, Devon Families, Tiverton, 2002, p.129, sold by Savilles estate agent February 2017, £1.5M <a class="external autonumber" href="https://search.savills.com/property-detail/gbetrsexs120254#/r/detail/GBETRSEXS120254" rel="nofollow">[14]</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Raleigh of Fardel arms per <a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole, Sir William</a> (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_de_la_Pole,_6th_Baronet" title="Sir John de la Pole, 6th Baronet">Sir John-William de la Pole</a> (ed.), London, 1791, p.499; Pedigree given in Vivian (pp.638-9) with same descent as Raleigh of Pilton, but with wrong arms</span>

<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vivian, p.638</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-93">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pole, p.321</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Welcombe" title="Welcombe">Welcombe</a> is a parish near <a href="/wiki/Hartland,_Devon" title="Hartland, Devon">Hartland</a> in North Devon, near the Cornish border. Other estates named "Welcombe" are listed in Pole, which may have been the residence of this family, with a very brief pedigree in Vivian, p.651 with no mention of parish. However, mention is made of <a href="/wiki/Week_St_Mary" title="Week St Mary">Week St Mary</a> (in Cornwall), 13 miles south of Welcombe near Hartland, and the Roache family originated in "Lesawnte" (<a href="/wiki/Lezant" title="Lezant">Lezant</a>?, Cornwall. Lysons, Magna Britannia, Cornwall, Extinct Gentry, states: "Roche or De la Rupe of Roche — traced to the reign of Richard I. Hals says, that this family became extinct, in the male line, in 1357; that Sir William Blundell, husband of the heiress, took the name of Roche, which continued till the reign of Henry VIII., when the last of the family left four daughters, three of whom married Fortescue, Penkevil, and Boscawen. The Roches had married heiresses of Trevelyan and Page, and a coheiress of Durant. Arms of Roche: — Sab. three roaches, two, one, nayant, Argent." The Devon family used a crescent as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Difference_(heraldry)" title="Difference (heraldry)">difference</a> of a second son. The name was thus <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Latinized_names" title="List of Latinized names">Latinized</a> to <i>de (la) Rupe</i> (Lat: rupes-is, "rock") "from the rock", inspired by the French word <i>la roche, le rocher</i>, "rock", from degraded Latin <i>rocca</i>, recorded in use 980 AD (Larousse Lexis, Paris, 1979, p.1654) from which the English word "rock" (Collins Dict)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Townhouse_(Great_Britain)" title="Townhouse (Great Britain)">townhouse</a> of <a href="/wiki/George_Rolle" title="George Rolle">George Rolle</a> (d.1552), where he died, comprising "messuage, garden and curtilage". It was <a href="/wiki/Feudal_land_tenure_in_England" title="Feudal land tenure in England">held</a> from the crown in <a href="/wiki/Burgage" title="Burgage">burgage</a>, worth 30 shillings. Details of Buckfast Place from his <a href="/wiki/Inquisition_post_mortem" title="Inquisition post mortem">inquisition post mortem</a> quoted in Byrne, Muriel St. Clare, (ed.) The Lisle Letters, 6 vols, University of Chicago Press, Chicago &amp; London, 1981, vol.1, Appendix 25, p.414. This house, later known as the "Abbot's Lodge", was destroyed in 1942 during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> bombing. It had been the townhouse of the Abbot of <a href="/wiki/Buckfast_Abbey" title="Buckfast Abbey">Buckfast Abbey</a>, which Abbey and much of its lands, apparently excluding the Abbot's Lodge, had been acquired following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">Dissolution of the Monasteries</a> by Sir <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Denys" title="Thomas Denys">Thomas Denys</a> (c.1477-1561) of <a href="/wiki/Holcombe_Burnell" title="Holcombe Burnell">Holcombe Burnell</a>, whose eventual heir (by coincidence) was the Rolle family. It was at the Abbot's Lodge that the Grand Duke of Tuscany was entertained by Sir John Rolle in 1669 and it remained in the Rolle family until 1737 when it was sold to the Rev. John Heskett.(Source:<a class="external autonumber" href="http://demolition-exeter.blogspot.co.uk/2010/09/town-house-of-abbots-of-buckfast.html" rel="nofollow">[15]</a>) A photograph of the arms of Sir Henry Rolle (1545-1625) in this building taken shortly before its destruction survives in: <i>Devon Notes &amp; Queries, Vol.9, 1916-17, pp.97-9: "Armorial Bearings at the Abbot's Lodge", The Close, Exeter</i>. Image see: <a href="/wiki/File:SirHenryRolle_(1545-1625)_1602Arms_AbbotsLodge_CathedralClose_Exeter.jpg" title="File:SirHenryRolle (1545-1625) 1602Arms AbbotsLodge CathedralClose Exeter.jpg">File:SirHenryRolle (1545-1625) 1602Arms AbbotsLodge CathedralClose Exeter.jpg</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vivian, p.517, inherited from Roope by Kirkham</span>
</li>

The family was descended from Degorie Thorne (second son of John Thorne of Thorne) who (circa 15th c.) married Margaret Seccombe, daughter and heiress of Thomas Seccombe of Seccombe, Devon</span>

<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As depicted in stained glass in east window of Shute Church, Devon, impaled by arms of Pole of Shute, representing the marriage of Sir Courtenay Pole, 2nd Baronet (1619-1695) and Urith Shapcott, daughter of Thomas Shapcott of Shapcott in the parish of Knowstone, Devon. Elsewhere the arms are shown with a chevron <i>or</i> (Barnstaple Church on Tucker monument), or without chevron (in Knowstone Church and in Molland Church). <li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole, Sir William</a> (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, Sir John-William de la Pole (ed.), London, 1791, p.502. <li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The "steward of the court of the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Bedford" title="Earl of Bedford">Earl of Bedford</a>" at Werrington (then in Devon, now in Cornwall) in about 1600 was John Twiggs, whose family pedigree is included in the 1620 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heraldic_Visitation" title="Heraldic Visitation">Heraldic Visitation</a> of Devon. <li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-123">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Richard Waltham (1560-1632) of Trehill, was <a href="/wiki/Recorder_of_Exeter" title="Recorder of Exeter">Recorder of Exeter</a> 1628-32. His elder brother Jeffrie Waltham (1558-1626) of Exeter, was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Exeter" title="Mayor of Exeter">Mayor of Exeter</a> in 1613 and 1626 and was married to Katherin Duck, a sister of <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Duck" title="Nicholas Duck">Nicholas Duck</a> (1570-1628), <a href="/wiki/Recorder_of_Exeter" title="Recorder of Exeter">Recorder of Exeter</a> (Vivian, pp.772;309); Their aunt Katherin Waltham was the mother of the Devon historian <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Westcote" title="Thomas Westcote">Thomas Westcote</a> (c.1567-c.1637). (Vivian, pp.772;778)</span>

<li id="cite_note-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-124">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pole, p.506, who blazons the arms as <i>Gules, a chevron between three fishes naiant argent</i>, thus with chevron <i>argent</i> not <i>or</i> and with the unnamed fish <i>naiant</i> not <i>hauriant</i>. These arms of Waye of Marsh are however sculpted (without tinctures) quartered by Kirkham of Blagdon in the 16th century Kirkham Chantry of Paignton Church, and show a chevron with fish <i>hauriant</i>, as per Vivian's blazon. Nicholas Kirkham (d.1516) of Blagdon married Jane Waye, daughter and heiress of Robert Waye of Marsh (Vivian, p.516, pedigree of Kirkham). These are similar to the arms displayed in Exeter Guildhall, Devon, of "John Waye, Sheriff (of Exeter) 1541", shown as <i>Gules, three lucies hauriant in fess argent</i>. They should be distinguished from the completely different arms of Way of St Giles-in-the-Wood, near Great Torrington in Devon, often called "de Via" (i.e. literally "from the way") arms, apparently later adopted by the Pollard family of Way and also by the Davie family (Davy baronets) of Creedy, Devon, which claim their original surname as <i>de Via</i>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Marsh in parish of Newton St Cyres per <a href="/wiki/John_Prince_(biographer)" title="John Prince (biographer)">Prince, John</a>, (1643–1723) The Worthies of Devon, 1810 edition, London, p.554</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-126"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-126">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Arms of "Treawin of Weare Giffard" per Pole, p.505; Arms of "Weare of Clyst Honiton" per Vivian, p.774. Quartered by Fortescue of Weare Giffard and Filleigh, see monumental brass in Filleigh Church of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Fortescue" title="Richard Fortescue">Richard Fortescue</a> (c. 1517–1570)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-127"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-127">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Hamilton_Rogers" title="William Henry Hamilton Rogers">William Henry Hamilton Rogers</a>, <i>Memorials of the West, Historical and Descriptive, Collected on the Borderland of Somerset, Dorset and Devon</i>, Exeter, 1888, pp.226-7</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-128"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-128">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Todd_Gray_(Devon_Historian)" title="Todd Gray (Devon Historian)">Gray, Todd</a>, (ed.), <i>Devon Household Accounts, 1627–59</i>, Devon and Cornwall Record Society, Part I, 1995, p.xxxvii <i>The Willougby Family and the Accounts of Leyhill</i></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-129"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-129">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">John Withie of Berry Narbor married Joane Jewel, a sister of <a href="/wiki/John_Jewel" title="John Jewel">John Jewel</a> (1522-1571), <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Salisbury" title="Bishop of Salisbury">Bishop of Salisbury</a>, born at Bowden in the parish of Berry Narbor (Vivian, pp.814, 505)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-130"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-130">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vivian, p.793: <i>Wolecot in parochia de Thrustelton</i></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pole, p.394</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-132">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Re Orchard, see: Pevsner, Nikolaus &amp; Cherry, Bridget, The Buildings of England: Devon, London, 2004, pp.535,613, who places it in parish of Thrushelton (near Lew Trenchard). The Visitations are clear this family resided in the parish of Lew Trenchard, and various monuments of the family exist in that parish church ("MI" per Vivian, p.799).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">James Woodrouffe (d.1609) of Barnstaple was <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Barnstaple" title="Mayor of Barnstaple">Mayor of Barnstaple</a> in 1605 (Vivian, p.802; Lamplugh, Lois, Barnstaple: Town on the Taw,  South Molton, 2002, p.156). His first wife was Jone Worth, a daughter of Pawle Worth, thrice Mayor of Barnstaple in 1577, 1592 and 1603, who signed a letted dated 8 April 1588 concerning the town's objection to having been ordered by the Privy Council to provide an excessive number of ships to meet the Spanish Armada. (Lamplugh, pp.50,156)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-134"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-134">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Blazon per Pole, p.509; These arms are visible on several escutcheons in Washfield Church. The arms are blazoned incorrectly as <i>beaked and legged gules</i> in Vivian, p.805, pedigree of Worth</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-135">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">Dissolution of the Monasteries</a> during the reign of King Henry VIII (1509-1547) John Wotton purchased the estate of Inglebourne from the crown, previously a possession of Buckfastleigh Abbey (Risdon, p.165)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-136">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Phillip Wyatt (d.1592) was steward and Town Clerk of Barnstaple, near Braunton. He had several sons, of whom Adam Wyatt (d.1611) was Town Clerk of Barnstaple from 1586 and left a detailed diary which provides valuable information on the town at this period. The identity of the diarist as Adam Wyatt was made by the Devon historian <a href="/wiki/Todd_Gray_(historian)" title="Todd Gray (historian)">Todd Gray</a>, although traditionally the diarist was thought to have been his brother Philip Wyatt (d.1608) (Lamplugh, Lois, <i>Barnstaple: Town on the Taw</i>, South Molton, 2002, p.45). Their elder brother Hugh Wyatt of Shillingford, married Lady Mary Bourchier, a daughter of <a href="/wiki/John_Bourchier,_2nd_Earl_of_Bath" title="John Bourchier, 2nd Earl of Bath">John Bourchier, 2nd Earl of Bath</a> (1499-1561), of nearby Tawstock Court, a highly influential figure in Barnstaple. Another brother, Thomas Wyatt, married Margaret Risdon, an aunt of <a href="/wiki/Tristram_Risdon" title="Tristram Risdon">Tristram Risdon</a> (d.1640) the Devon historian. (Vivian, pp.823, 107, 648). Pole, p.508, gives the arms of "Wiatt of Shillingford" slightly differently as: <i>Azure, a chief gules over-all a horse-brake (barnacle) argent</i></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-137">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Bindon branch of Wyke used their maternal arms of Burnell, having inherited that estate from an heiress of that family (Pole, p.243; Woodger, L.S., biography of <i>Wyke, Roger (d.c.1467), of Bindon in Axmouth, Devon</i>, published in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Parliament" title="History of Parliament">History of Parliament</a>: House of Commons 1386-1421, ed. J.S. Roskell, L. Clark, C. Rawcliffe., 1993 <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.historyofparliamentonline.org/volume/1386-1421/member/wyke-roger-1467" rel="nofollow">[20]</a>)</i></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-138">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pole, Sir William (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, Sir John-William de la Pole (ed.), London, 1791, p.507</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Arms inherited from the Bushel family of Bradley/Teignwick (Pole, p.472)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Todd_Gray_(Devon_Historian)" title="Todd Gray (Devon Historian)">Gray, Todd</a> &amp; Rowe, Margery (Eds.), Travels in Georgian Devon: The Illustrated Journals of The Reverend <a href="/wiki/John_Swete" title="John Swete">John Swete</a>, 1789-1800, 4 vols., Tiverton, 1999, Vol 2, p.164; Pevsner, p.556</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-141"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-141">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Swete, Vol.2, p.164</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-142"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-142">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Per research conducted by Sheila Yeo of the Yeo Society <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.yeosociety.com/heraldry/yeo%20evidence.htm" rel="nofollow">[21]</a>, based on stained glass depictions of Yeo arms in churches of Petrockstowe (Yeo of Heanton Satchville) and Hatherleigh (Yeo of Hatherleigh) both in Devon. The ducks are described as of various breeds by different sources. Heraldic sources give contradictory tinctures: <i>Argent, a chevron between three shovelers sable</i> (Vivian, Lt.Col. J.L., (Ed.) The Visitations of the County of Devon: Comprising the Heralds' Visitations of 1531, 1564 &amp; 1620, Exeter, 1895, p.834) and <i>Argent, a chevron between three mallards azure</i> (<a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole, Sir William</a> (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, Sir John-William de la Pole (ed.), London, 1791, p.510)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The return made in 1620 to the heralds was signed by Robert Yonge (d.1636) of Colebrooke, 4th son of Thomas Younge of <a href="/wiki/Sturminster_Newton" title="Sturminster Newton">Sturminster Newton</a> in Dorset. Robert's nephew was Thomas Yonge (of Child, Ockford) who married Bridget Seymer, a sister of Sir Robert Seymer (d.1624) of Hanford in Dorset, a Teller in the King's Exchequer, knighted at Greenwich Palace on 19 February 1619 (Burke, John, <i>A Genealogical and Heraldic Dictionary of the Landed Gentry of Great Britain and Ireland</i>, Vol. 2 (M-Z), London, 1846, p.1216 <a class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=FlI4AQAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA1216&amp;lpg=PA1216&amp;dq=Seymour+Hanford+Dorset&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=UjT-Ig7fWb&amp;sig=T6v5O5oxZ6p0GRP-vabwhSPmdDU&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwig4JPPzarXAhXCNhoKHSaeBWY4ChDoAQhOMAg#v=onepage&amp;q=Seymour%20Hanford%20Dorset&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">[22]</a>)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://forebears.co.uk/england/devon/colebrooke" rel="nofollow">Kelly's Directory of Devon, 1902</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-145"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-145">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/William_Pole_(antiquary)" title="William Pole (antiquary)">Pole, Sir William</a> (d.1635), Collections Towards a Description of the County of Devon, Sir John-William de la Pole (ed.), London, 1791, pp.467-510</span>
</li>
</ol></div>
